Sulh with Acknowledgment: Legal Treatment as a Sale
Commentary on sulh with iqrar being like a sale, with three specific consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that sulh ma'a iqrar involving property exchange is treated as a sale and identify the three specific sale rulings that apply to it.

Core Idea
When property is exchanged in a compromise, meaning overrides form — it becomes a sale.

You might think that a compromise settlement (sulh) is always a distinct contract from a sale. However, Hanafi fiqh looks at the underlying reality: if the sulh involves an exchange of property for property by mutual consent, it legally functions as a sale. In this passage, the commentator on Al-Wiqayah expands on the matn's statement that the first type of sulh is 'like a sale' and draws out three practical consequences: pre-emption (shuf'a), the right to return for a defect, and the option of sight. Let's trace the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage begins by stating that sulh with acknowledgment (sulh ma'a iqrar) when it involves property for property is considered a sale. Write down the legal ruling: it is treated as a sale for all purposes.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The commentator gives the 'secret' (sirr): sulh is interpreted according to the contract most similar to it. Since a sale involves the exchange of property for property with mutual consent, sulh that has this meaning is governed by sale law. This is a qiyas jaliy based on the illa of property exchange.
Qiyas is the proof (dalil) for this treatment.
3
Apply the principle to subcategories
The passage breaks down cases based on whether the property is of the same type or different, and whether the amount is less, equal, or more. Identify which subcategories result in sale (different type; same type with excess) and which do not (hatt/ibra', qabd/istifa').
This shows that the treatment as sale is not absolute but depends on the nature of the exchange.
4
Examine the three consequences
The commentator explicitly lists three sale rulings that apply to this type of sulh: (1) pre-emption (shuf'a) for real estate, (2) right to return for a defect (radd bi 'ayb), and (3) option of sight (khiyar ru'ya). For each, note the scenario and why the ruling applies.
These are applications of the general principle.
5
Synthesize the legal reasoning
Conclude that the Hanafi method emphasizes ma'ani (meanings) over suwar (forms). This is a consistent theme: a gift with a condition of compensation is sale, a guarantee with exoneration becomes hawala, etc. The student should be able to articulate this method.
This principle is key in many Hanafi rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] قوله : فالأول كبيع ؛ يعني أن الصلح مع إقرار إن وقع عن مال بمال فيعتبر بيعاً ؛ لوجود معنى البيع فيه، وهو مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضي فيجري فيه أحكام البيع كالشفعة وغيرها، مما ذكره المصنف . والسر فيه : إنّ الأصل في الصلح أن يحمل على أشبه العقود له فيجري عليه أحكامه ؛ لأنّ العبرة للمعاني دون الصور ؛ ولهذا جعلت الهبة بشرط العوض بيعاً ، والكفالة بشرط براءة الأصيل حوالة والحوالة بشرط عدم براءة الأصيل كفالة. فإذا وقع الصلح عن مال بمال ينظر : إن وقع على خلاف جنسه أو على جنسه ، فعلى الأول : هو بيع وشراء وعلى الثاني : فلا يخلو إمّا أن يكون بأقل من المدعى، أو بمثله، أو بأكثر منه، فالأوّل حط وابراء ، والثاني قبض واستيفاء، والثالث فضل وربا. [٢]قوله : فيجري فيه الشفعة في العقار ؛ بأن كانت الدعوى في دار في يد رجل قد أقر له بها، فصالح المدعي على مال معين دفعه إليه ، فهذا في معنى البيع، وللجار أن يطالبه الشفعة فيه. [٣] قوله : والردّ بعيب ؛ بأن كان بدل الصلح عبداً مثلاً ، فوجد المدعي فيه عيباً فله أن يرده ؛ لأنه اعتبر بيعاً. ٤١ قوله : وخيار رؤية ؛ بأن لم ير المصالح ما وقع عليه الصلح وقت الصلح، ثم رآه فله الخيار فيه، كما في شراء ما لم يره.
[1] His statement: 'The first is like a sale' means that sulh with acknowledgment, if it occurs as property in exchange for property, is considered a sale because the meaning of sale exists in it—that is, the exchange of property for property by mutual consent. Thus, the rulings of sale apply to it, such as pre-emption and other matters mentioned by the author. The underlying reason is that the principle in sulh is to treat it as the contract most similar to it, and apply its rulings, because consideration is given to meanings, not forms. For this reason, a gift with a condition of compensation is made a sale, a guarantee with a condition of the exoneration of the principal is made a transfer of debt, and a transfer of debt with a condition of the non-exoneration of the principal is made a guarantee. When sulh occurs as property for property, it is examined: if it occurs for something of a different type or of the same type. In the first case, it is a sale and purchase. In the second, it is either for less than the claimed amount, equal to it, or more than it. The first is a reduction and release, the second is receipt and collection, and the third is surplus and riba. [2] His statement: 'Pre-emption applies in it' regarding real estate: for example, if the claim was for a house in the possession of a man who acknowledged it to him, and the claimant settled for a specific sum paid to him, then this is in the meaning of a sale, and the neighbor has the right to demand pre-emption in it. [3] His statement: 'Return due to defect' : for example, if the substitute in the sulh was a slave, and the claimant finds a defect in him, he has the right to return him, because it is considered a sale. [4] His statement: 'Option of sight' : if the person settling did not see the subject of the sulh at the time of the settlement, then later saw it, he has the option in it, just as in the purchase of that which he has not seen.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn's statement 'فالأول كبيع' (the first is like a sale). The commentator explains that when sulh with acknowledgment (sulh ma'a iqrar) involves an exchange of property for property, it is legally treated as a sale. The reason is that the essential meaning—mutual exchange of property—is present, and in Islamic law, consideration is given to meanings (ma'ani) rather than mere forms (suwar). The commentator gives analogous examples: a gift with a condition of compensation is a sale; a guarantee (kafala) with a condition of the principal's exoneration becomes a transfer of debt (hawala); and a hawala with a condition of the principal's continued liability becomes a kafala. The commentator then details the subcategories: if the sulh is for property of a different type, it is a full sale; if the same type, it may be a reduction (hatt wa ibra'), receipt (qabd wa istifa'), or excess which is riba. Then the commentator expands three specific consequences: (1) pre-emption (shuf'a) applies in real estate, (2) the right to return for a defect (radd bi 'ayb) exists, and (3) the option of sight (khiyar ru'ya) applies. All these are because the sulh is governed by the law of sale.

Key Terms
الصلح مع إقرار (al-sulh ma'a iqrar): A compromise settlement where the defendant acknowledges the claim and then agrees to settle for less or different property.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Pre-emption right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the property at the price agreed upon between the seller and buyer.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of sight: a buyer who purchases something they have not seen has the right to revoke the sale upon seeing the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, when sulh with iqrar involves an exchange of property for property, which contract is it legally analogous to?
A) Hibah (gift)
B) Ijarah (lease)
C) Bay' (sale)
D) Kafalah (guarantee)

Key Takeaway
Sulh ma'a iqrar involving property exchange is legally a sale; hence pre-emption, defect return, and sight option apply.

Ignorance of the Substitute and Istihqaq in Sulh
Commentary on invalidating conditions and classification of sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on jahalat al-badal to classify a sulh as valid or invalid, and explain the effect of istihqaq on the compensation.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the substitute invalidates sulh only when delivery is required; if no delivery, ignorance is permitted.

Sulh (settlement) is a commendable way to end disputes, but it has strict conditions. One key condition is that the substitute (badal) must be known if it is to be delivered. This lesson examines the commentator's detailed classification of sulh based on knowledge of the two items, and introduces the rule for when the claimed property is proven to belong to a third party (istihqaq).

Guided Path
1
Understand the nullifying effect of jahalat al-badal
The passage explains that ignorance of the substitute (badal) invalidates sulh because it leads to dispute. However, this is not absolute; it depends on whether delivery of the substitute is required.
Ignorance of the subject of settlement (musalah 'anhu) may be excused if it is simply being dropped.
2
Classify sulh into three categories based on knowledge
The commentator identifies: (1) known for known, (2) unknown for unknown, (3) unknown for known. Each has sub-cases based on whether delivery is required.
Unknown for unknown is valid only if no delivery; unknown for known is valid only if no delivery.
3
Apply the rule: jahala invalidates only when delivery is required
The key principle: wherever delivery and receipt (tasleem wa tasallum) are required, ignorance leads to dispute and invalidates sulh. Where delivery is not required, ignorance does not lead to dispute.
Memorize: 'In every case where delivery and receipt are not required, ignorance does not lead to dispute, so it does not prevent validity.'
4
Analyze the beginning of the istihqaq discussion
The passage starts to address what happens if the claimed property in a sulh with iqrar is proven to belong to another. The compensation must be adjusted proportionally.
The full rule will be covered later; for now note that the claimant must return part of the compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] قوله : والشرط ; أي وخيار الشرط، بأن تصالحا على شيء، فشرط أحدهما الخيار لنفسه، فإنّه جاز؛ لأنه من أحكام البيع. [٢]قوله : ويفسده جهالة البدل ; فإنَّ جهالة البدل تفضي إلى المنازعة، فإنَّ البدل يحتاج إلى قبضه، فلا بد من إعلامه بحيث لا يبقى فيه منازعة بينهما بخلاف جهالة المصالح عنه ، كما يقول السفير بين المتخاصمين : كلّ دعوى لك على فلان صالحة على هذا المقدار ; لأنه يسقط ، واعلم أنَّ الصلح لا يخلو : ١. إما أن يكون عن معلوم على معلوم، بأن ادعى حقاً معلوماً في يد رجل فصالح المدعى عليه فإنّه جائز. وجهين : ٢. أو يكون عن مجهول على مجهول، وهو على وجـ الأول : إنه لا يحتاجُ فيه إلى التسليم والتسلم بأن ادعى حقاً في دار في يد رجل ، ولم يسلّم، وادعى المدعى عليه حقاً في أرض في يد المدعي ولم يُسلّم، فأصطلحا على أن يترك كلُّ واحدٍ منهما ما ادعاه على صاحبه وهو جائز. من أحدهما والثاني : إنّه يحتاجُ فيه إلى التسليم والتسلم بأن اصطلحا على أن يدفع أ. عند نفسه مالاً ولم يبينه على أن يترك الآخر دعواه ، أو على أن يسلم إليه ما ادعاه ، فإنّه لا يجوز. . أو يكون عن مجهول على معلوم، وهو أيضاً على وجهين : الأول : إنه يحتاج إلى تسليمه فهو غير جائز. والثاني : إنه لا يحتاج فهو جائز ، ففي كل موضع لا يحتاج فيه إلى التسليم والتسلّم، فالجهالة فيه لا تفضي إلى المنازعة، فلا تمنع جواز الصلح، وفي كل موضع يحتاجُ فيه إلى التسليم والتسلم، فالجهالة فيه تفضي إلى المنازعة، فتمنع جواز الصلح، فاحفظه فإنّه نافع لك. [٣] قوله : ما استحق... الخ ; يعني إنّ المدعى وهو المصالح عنه في الصلح مع الإقرار
[1] His statement: 'And the condition' means the option of stipulation. For example, if they settled on something, and one of them stipulated an option for himself, then it is permitted, because it is from the rulings of sale. [2] His statement: 'And ignorance of the substitute invalidates it' : because ignorance of the substitute leads to dispute. The substitute requires delivery, so it must be specified such that no dispute remains between them, unlike ignorance of the subject of settlement. As the mediator between litigants says: 'Every claim you have against so-and-so is settled for this amount,' because it is dropped. Know that sulh is not free from: 1. It may be for known in exchange for known, such as if he claimed a known right in the possession of a man, and the defendant settled, then it is permissible. 2. Or it may be for unknown in exchange for unknown, and this is of two types: The first: it does not require delivery and receipt, such as if he claimed a right in a house in a man's possession without delivery, and the defendant claimed a right in land in the claimant's possession without delivery, and they agreed that each would abandon his claim against the other—this is permissible. The second: it requires delivery and receipt, such as if they agreed that one of them would pay some unspecified money to abandon his claim, or to hand over what he claimed—this is not permissible. 3. Or it may be for unknown in exchange for known, and this is also of two types: The first: it requires delivery, so it is not permissible. The second: it does not require delivery, so it is permissible. In every case where delivery and receipt are not required, ignorance does not lead to dispute, so it does not prevent the validity of sulh. In every case where delivery and receipt are required, ignorance leads to dispute, so it prevents the validity of sulh. So remember this, for it is beneficial to you. [3] His statement: 'What is proven to belong to another...' means that the claimed property, which is the subject of settlement in sulh with acknowledgment,
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage expands on the conditions that invalidate sulh and the effects of istihqaq (proven ownership by a third party). The commentator first explains that stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) is permissible because it is a ruling of sale. Then he discusses the nullifying effect of ignorance (jahala) of the substitute (badal). Ignorance leads to dispute, so it invalidates the sulh, but ignorance of the subject of settlement (musalah 'anhu) may be excused. The commentator provides a detailed classification of sulh based on knowledge of the two items (known/unknown) and whether delivery is required. The rule is: if delivery is required, ignorance invalidates; if not, ignorance does not invalidate. Finally, the commentator begins to explain the effect of istihqaq: when the claimed property is proven to belong to a third party, the settlement is adjusted proportionally. The text cuts off, but the general principle is that the claimant returns a portion of the compensation corresponding to the portion proven to belong to another.

Key Terms
جهالة البدل (jahalat al-badal): Ignorance of the substitute (the property being paid) in a sulh agreement.
استحقاق المدعى (istihqaq al-mudda'a): The situation where the claimed property is proven to rightfully belong to someone other than the defendant or claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does ignorance of the substitute (badal) invalidate the sulh?
A) Always invalidates
B) Only when the subject of settlement is unknown
C) When delivery and receipt (tasleem wa tasallum) are required
D) Only when the sulh is with iqrar

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of sulh hinges on whether the substitute is known when delivery is required; ignorance leads to dispute and invalidates the agreement.

The Option of Stipulation in Sulh
Ruling statement on khiyar al-shart in sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart in sulh and explain the reasoning by analogy to sale.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is valid in sulh because sulh is analogous to sale.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text clarifies that stipulating an option to rescind a settlement (sulh) is permissible. The reasoning is rooted in the established permissibility of options in sales. Understanding this ruling helps you grasp how the Hanafi school extends principles across similar contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the stipulation
Determine what type of contract is being discussed (sulh) and what stipulation is added (khiyar al-shart).
2
State the ruling
The text says it is permissible (jā'iz). Confirm the hukm level: mubah.
3
Locate the reason
The reason given is 'because it is from the rulings of sale'. This is the dalil via qiyas.
4
Recognize the analogy
Sulh is analogized to sale (bay') in Hanafi fiqh regarding options. This is a key principle.
The analogy is general; not all sale rules necessarily apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط، [1] قوله : والشرط ; أي وخيار الشرط، بأن تصالحا على شيء، فشرط أحدهما الخيار لنفسه، فإنّه جاز؛ لأنه من أحكام البيع.
And condition. [1] He said: 'And the condition'; meaning the option of stipulation: that they settle on something, then one of them stipulates the option for himself, then it is permissible, because it is from the rulings of sale.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the permissibility of stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) in a contract of sulh (compromise/settlement). The matn simply says 'and condition' referring to the option of stipulation. The commentary clarifies that if two parties make a sulh and one of them stipulates a condition of option (e.g., the right to rescind within a specified period), it is valid (jā'iz). The reason given is that sulh is treated like a sale (bay') in this regard, and option conditions are valid in sales according to the Hanafi school. Thus, the ruling is that khiyar al-shart is permissible in sulh contracts.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): Here, 'al-shart' refers specifically to khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), i.e., the right to rescind the contract within a specified period.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation, where one or both parties reserve the right to cancel the contract within a known period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on stipulating a condition of option (khiyar al-shart) in a contract of sulh?
A) It is invalid
B) It is valid
C) It is disliked
D) It is mandatory

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is permissible in sulh because sulh is analogized to sale in Hanafi fiqh.

Ignorance of the Substitute Invalidates Sulh
Ruling with rational proof and classification of sulh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ignorance of the substitute and ignorance of the subject matter in sulh, and apply the rule that ignorance invalidates only when delivery is required.

Core Idea
Ignorance of what must be delivered invalidates; ignorance of what is dropped does not.

In sulh (settlement) contracts, the Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between the substitute (badal) that is given and the claim (musālah 'anhu) that is dropped. Ignorance of the substitute leads to disputes over delivery, making the contract invalid. However, ignorance of the exact claim being dropped is tolerated because no delivery is involved. This lesson unpacks the rationale and classification provided in the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its cause
The matn states 'ignorance of the substitute invalidates it'. The commentary provides the cause: it leads to dispute because the substitute requires delivery. Understand this causal link (talil).
This is a ruling with proof based on rational reasoning (talil), not a textual proof.
2
Contrast with ignorance of the subject matter
The author contrasts jahālat al-badal with jahālat al-musālah 'anhu. The latter does not invalidate because the claim is dropped, not delivered. Learn the distinction through the mediator example.
The mediator says 'every claim you have against so-and-so is settled for this amount.' The claim is dropped, so its exact nature need not be known.
3
Analyze the classification of sulh
The text divides sulh into three categories based on knowledge of the substitute and subject matter: known/known, unknown/unknown, unknown/known. Each has sub-cases based on whether delivery is required. Trace each sub-case and its ruling.
Use the provided table in conditions_pillars to organize the cases.
4
Apply the governing principle
The final principle: whenever delivery and receipt (taslīm wa tasallum) are required, ignorance invalidates; when not required, ignorance does not invalidate. Apply this to hypothetical scenarios.
Memorize the principle as a concise rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفسده جهالة البدل. [2] قوله : ويفسده جهالة البدل ; فإنَّ جهالة البدل تفضي إلى المنازعة، فإنَّ البدل يحتاج إلى قبضه، فلا بد من إعلامه بحيث لا يبقى فيه منازعة بينهما بخلاف جهالة المصالح عنه ، كما يقول السفير بين المتخاصمين : كلّ دعوى لك على فلان صالحة على هذا المقدار ; لأنه يسقط ، واعلم أنَّ الصلح لا يخلو : ١. إما أن يكون عن معلوم على معلوم، بأن ادعى حقاً معلوماً في يد رجل فصالح المدعى عليه فإنّه جائز. وجهين : ٢. أو يكون عن مجهول على مجهول، وهو على وجهين : الأول : إنه لا يحتاجُ فيه إلى التسليم والتسلم بأن ادعى حقاً في دار في يد رجل ، ولم يسلّم، وادعى المدعى عليه حقاً في أرض في يد المدعي ولم يُسلّم، فأصطلحا على أن يترك كلُّ واحدٍ منهما ما ادعاه على صاحبه وهو جائز. والثاني : إنّه يحتاجُ فيه إلى التسليم والتسلم بأن اصطلحا على أن يدفع أ. عند نفسه مالاً ولم يبينه على أن يترك الآخر دعواه ، أو على أن يسلم إليه ما ادعاه ، فإنّه لا يجوز. . أو يكون عن مجهول على معلوم، وهو أيضاً على وجهين : الأول : إنه يحتاج إلى تسليمه فهو غير جائز. والثاني : إنه لا يحتاج فهو جائز ، ففي كل موضع لا يحتاج فيه إلى التسليم والتسلّم، فالجهالة فيه لا تفضي إلى المنازعة، فلا تمنع جواز الصلح، وفي كل موضع يحتاجُ فيه إلى التسليم والتسلم، فالجهالة فيه تفضي إلى المنازعة، فتمنع جواز الصلح، فاحفظه فإنّه نافع لك.
And ignorance of the substitute invalidates it. [2] He said: 'And ignorance of the substitute invalidates it' because ignorance of the substitute leads to dispute; indeed, the substitute requires delivery, so it must be made known in a way that no dispute remains between them, unlike ignorance of the subject matter of settlement. As the mediator between disputants says: 'Every claim you have against so-and-so is settled for this amount' because it drops (the claim). Know that sulh is not free from three types: 1. Either it is from known to known, such as if someone claims a known right in the hand of a man, so the defendant settles; then it is permissible. 2. Or it is from unknown to unknown, and it is of two types: the first: that it does not require delivery and receipt, such as if someone claims a right in a house in the hand of a man, and has not delivered, and the defendant claims a right in a land in the hand of the plaintiff, and has not delivered, so they agree that each leaves what he claims on the other; this is permissible. The second: that it requires delivery and receipt, such as if they agree that he pays something from himself without specifying it, on condition that the other leaves his claim; or that he delivers to him what he claimed; then it is not permissible. Or it is from unknown to known, and it also has two types: the first: that it requires delivery, so it is not permissible. The second: that it does not require delivery, so it is permissible. So in every place where delivery and receipt are not required, the ignorance there does not lead to dispute, so it does not prevent the permissibility of sulh. And in every place where delivery and receipt are required, the ignorance there leads to dispute, so it prevents the permissibility of sulh. So memorize it, for it is beneficial to you.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. The matn states that ignorance of the substitute (badal) invalidates the sulh contract. The commentary explains the rationale: ignorance of the substitute leads to dispute (munāza'ah) because the substitute must be delivered; thus it must be known precisely. In contrast, ignorance of the subject matter (musālah 'anhu) does not invalidate the contract because the subject matter is dropped (sāqit) and does not require delivery. The mediator's example illustrates that if the mediator says 'every claim you have against so-and-so is settled for this amount,' the claim is dropped, so ignorance of the detail of the claim is acceptable. The commentary then classifies sulh into three categories based on knowledge of the subject matter and substitute: (1) known for known: always permissible; (2) unknown for unknown: sub-divided into whether delivery is required or not; if no delivery required (e.g., mutual dropping of claims), it is permissible; if delivery is required but the amount is unspecified, it is not permissible; (3) unknown for known: similarly sub-divided based on delivery requirement. The key principle is: wherever delivery and receipt are not required, ignorance does not lead to dispute and thus does not invalidate sulh. Where delivery is required, ignorance leads to dispute and invalidates.

Key Terms
جهالة البدل (jahālat al-badal): Ignorance of the substitute (compensation) in a sulh contract; it invalidates the contract because it leads to dispute over delivery.
جهالة المصالح عنه (jahālat al-musālah 'anhu): Ignorance of the subject matter of settlement (the claim that is dropped); it does not invalidate sulh because it is dropped and not delivered.
تسليم وتسلم (taslīm wa tasallum): Delivery and receipt; required in contracts where a physical or legal transfer occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of ignorance invalidates a sulh contract?
A) Ignorance of the substitute (badal) when delivery is required
B) Ignorance of the subject matter (musalah anhu) when it is dropped
C) Both A and B
D) Neither A nor B

Key Takeaway
In sulh, the ruling hinges on delivery: ignorance invalidates only when the object of ignorance must be delivered, not when it is simply dropped.

Proportional Recovery upon Istihqaq in Sulh
Rules when part of subject matter or compensation is reclaimed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of proportional recovery when part or all of the subject matter or compensation in sulh is reclaimed, and apply it to given scenarios.

Core Idea
When reclaimed property is taken back, the party who gave up value recovers proportionally—each side's consideration mirrors the other's loss.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on istihqaq (reclamation by a rightful owner) in a sulh (compromise) contract. When a third party proves ownership of all or part of the subject matter or the compensation, the affected party has a right to proportional recovery from the other party. Using a clear example, we will see how this principle is applied symmetrically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sulh contract that is valid. The ruling concerns what happens if a third party reclaims part or all of the subject matter or compensation that was transferred.
The sulh itself is sahih; the issue is post-contract adjustment.
2
Understand the scenario
Know the roles: claimant (mudda'i) and defendant (mudda'a 'alayh). In sulh with admission (iqrar), the defendant pays compensation and receives the claimed property. Example: Zayd claims a house from Amr; Amr admits and pays 100 dirhams; the house goes to Amr.
The example is with iqrar but the rule applies more broadly.
3
Apply the principle of reciprocity
Each party's transfer is consideration for the other's. If a third party reclaims part of the house, Amr recovers that proportion of the 100 dirhams. If half the house is reclaimed, Amr recovers 50 dirhams. If the whole house is reclaimed, Amr recovers all 100 dirhams. The same applies if the compensation is reclaimed: Zayd recovers a proportion of the house.
The recovery is exactly proportional to the part reclaimed.
4
Note the symmetry
The rule applies identically whether the loss is on the subject matter side or the compensation side. This symmetry is the key legal point.
This mirrors the rule in sales (istihqaq in bay').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[3] قوله : ما استحق... الخ ; يعني إنّ المدعى وهو المصالح عنه في الصلح مع الإقرار إن كان مستحقاً سواء كان كلاً أو بعضاً رجع المدعى عليه على المدعي بكل اليد إن كان المستحق كله، أو بعضه إن كان المستحق بعضه. وصورته : إنَّ زيداً مثلاً ادَّعى داراً في يد عمرو ، فأقر عمرو وصالح زيداً على مئة درهم، فصارت المئة في يد زيد، والدار في يد عمرو ، ثمَّ استحق نصفُ الدَّارِ أو كلّها يرجع عمرو على زيد بخمسين درهماً في الأولى، وبمئة درهم في الثانية. وإن استحق بعض البدل أو كله رجع المدعي على المدعى عليه بكل المصالح عنه أو بعضه ; لأنَّ كلَّ واحدٍ منهما عوض عن الآخر، فأيهما أُخِذَ منه بالاستحقاق رجع بما دفع إن كلاً فبالكل، وإن بعضاً فالبعض.
[3] He said: 'What is reclaimed... etc.'; meaning the claimed property, which is the subject matter in sulh with admission, if it is reclaimed, whether wholly or partially, the defendant (the one against whom the claim was made) recovers from the plaintiff (the claimant) the full handed-over compensation if the whole is reclaimed, or a portion if a portion is reclaimed. Its example: Zayd, for instance, claimed a house in the hand of Amr, and Amr admitted and settled with Zayd for one hundred dirhams, so the hundred came into Zayd's hand, and the house into Amr's hand. Then if half the house or all of it is reclaimed, Amr recovers from Zayd fifty dirhams in the first case, and one hundred dirhams in the second. And if part of the substitute or all of it is reclaimed, the plaintiff recovers from the defendant all or part of the subject matter; because each one is consideration for the other. So whichever one has something taken from him by reclamation, he recovers what he paid, if wholly then wholly, if partially then partially.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an example from the Hanafi school. It explains the effects when part of the subject matter (musālah 'anhu) or the compensation (badal) is reclaimed by a rightful third party (istihqāq). The commentary defines 'al-mudda'a' as the subject matter in sulh with iqrār (admission). If the subject matter is reclaimed, the defendant (who admitted and paid compensation) recovers from the plaintiff a proportional amount of the compensation. For example, if Zayd claims a house from Amr, Amr admits and settles for 100 dirhams, then half the house is reclaimed (proving it belonged to someone else), Amr recovers 50 dirhams from Zayd. If the whole house is reclaimed, Amr recovers all 100 dirhams. Conversely, if part of the compensation is reclaimed (e.g., the 100 dirhams were partially someone else's), the plaintiff recovers a proportional share of the subject matter. The principle is that each party's payment is consideration for the other; if a third party takes something from one, that party recovers proportionally from the other.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Reclamation by a rightful owner, meaning that part or all of the property transferred in sulh is proven to belong to a third party.
المدعى (al-mudda‘ā): The claimed property; in this context, the subject matter of the sulh that was originally claimed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If after a sulh contract, half of the subject matter (claimed property) is reclaimed by a rightful owner, how much does the defendant recover from the plaintiff?
A) Half of the compensation paid
B) The full compensation
C) Nothing
D) The full subject matter

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a valid sulh contract survives reclamation, but the affected party recovers proportionally from the other party because each consideration is reciprocal.

Rulings on Istihqaq of Claimed Property or Compensation in Sulh
Explains rules when third party claims the subject matter or compensation in sulh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rules when a third party claims the property or compensation in a sulh, apply them to examples, and distinguish the case where sulh uses sale wording.

Core Idea
If the claimed property is taken, plaintiff returns compensation and sues the third party; if the compensation is taken, he reverts to his claim.

When a third party (mustahiqq) proves ownership of either the property that was the subject of a sulh or the compensation paid by the defendant, the settlement is disturbed. The Hanafi school provides clear rules to restore justice: the plaintiff must either return the compensation and pursue the true owner, or revert to his original claim. This lesson unpacks these rulings and their rationales, including an important exception when the settlement is phrased as a sale.

Guided Path
1
Classify the two scenarios
Identify the two distinct cases in the passage: when the claimed property (mudda'a) is taken by a third party, and when the compensation (badal) is taken.
The text uses the terms 'mudda'a' (claimed property) and 'badal' (compensation).
2
State the plaintiff's obligation in each case
For mudda'a taken: plaintiff returns the compensation to the defendant and litigates with the third party. For badal taken: plaintiff reverts to his original claim against the defendant.
The return is proportional to what was taken; if part is taken, only that part's value is returned.
3
Analyze the rationale
The defendant paid compensation only to remove litigation; if the property is taken, his purpose fails, so he gets his money back. The plaintiff abandoned his claim only to receive the compensation; if it is taken, his basis for abandoning the claim disappears.
This prevents unjust enrichment and preserves the defendant's right to a defense.
4
Compare with sulh using sale wording
If the sulh is phrased as a sale, the defendant's agreement implies acknowledgment of the plaintiff's ownership. Thus, if the compensation is taken, the plaintiff claims the property itself from the defendant, not just the original claim.
This distinction shows how the form of the contract changes the legal outcome.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., plaintiff claims a car, settles for $5,000, then a third party proves ownership of the car), identify which scenario applies and state the obligations.
Practice builds fluency in applying the rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما استحق من المدعى رد المدعي حصته من العوض، ورجع بالخصومة فيه، وما استحق من البدل من يد المدعي رجع إلى الدعوى في كله، أو بعضه (وما اسْتُحِق من المدعى ردّ المدعي حصته من العوض، ورجع بالخصومة فيه) : أي يخاصمُ المُسْتَحِقُّ فيما استحقه، (وما استحق من البدل من يد المدعي رجع إلى الدعوى في كله أو بعضه) : أي إن استحق بعض البدل من يد المدعي رَجَعَ إلى دعوى حصة ما استحق من المصالح . عنه ، وإن استحق كلَّه رَجَعَ إلى دعوى الكل، وفي الصلح مع الإقرار إذا استحق البدل رَجَعَ إلى المُبْدَل ؛ لوجود إقرار المدعى عليه ، وفي السكوتِ والإنكار رَجَعَ إلى دعوى المبدل. [1]قوله : وما استحق...الخ ؛ يعني ما استحق من المدعى كلا أو بعضاً في صورة الصلح مع سكوت أو إنكار، يردُّ المدعي على المدعى عليه حصته من البدل، ويرجعُ المدعي بالخصومة مع المستحق فيما استحقه كلاً كان أو بعضاً. وصورته : إنَّ رجلاً ادّعى داراً في يد رجل فأنكر أو سكت، ثمَّ صالح عنها على مئة درهم، فصارت المئة في يد المدعي، والدار في يد المدعى عليه، ثم استحق كل الدار أو بعضه، فالمدعي يرد المئة إذا استحق كل الدار، أو الخمسين إن استحق نصفها للمدعى عليه، ويرجع بالخصومة في الدار إلى المستحق؛ لأنه أخذه على زعمِهِ عوضاً عما ادعى. فإذا استحق ذلك يرجع عليه المدعى عليه بناءً على زعمه، كأنه اشتراه منه ؛ ولأنَّ المدعى عليه لم يدفع العوض إلا ليدفع خصومةً عن نفسه، وليبق المدعى في يده من غير خصومة أحد، فإذا استحق لم يحصل له المقصود). (٢) قوله : وما استحق من البدل...الخ ؛ أي وما استحق من البدل كلاً أو بعضاً يرجع المدعي إلى دعواه في قدره، فإن استحق الكل يرجع إلى الكل، وإن استحق البعض يرجع إلى البعض ؛ لأن المدعي لم يترك الدعوى إلا ليسلم له البدل، فإذا لم يسلم له رجع بالمبدل وهو الدعوى. بخلاف ما إذا وقع الصلح بلفظ البيع، بأن قال أحدهما : بعتك هذا الشيء بهذا ، وقال الآخر : اشتريت، حيث يرجع المدعي . عند الاستحقاق على المدعى عليه بالمدعى نفسه لا بالدعوى ؛ لأن إقدام المدعى عليه على المبايعة إقرار منه بأن المدعى ملك المدعي فلا يعتبر إنكاره بخلاف الصلح ؛ لأنه لم يوجد منه ما يدل على أنه أقر بالملك له ، إذ الصلح قد يقع لدفع الخصومة. ذكره في «التبيين»)، وغيره.
And whatever of the claimed property is taken (by a third party), the plaintiff returns his share of the compensation, and he returns to litigation regarding it. And whatever of the compensation is taken from the hand of the plaintiff, he returns to the claim in its entirety or part of it. (And whatever of the claimed property is taken, the plaintiff returns his share of the compensation and returns to litigation regarding it): i.e. he litigates with the claimant regarding what he claimed. (And whatever of the compensation is taken from the hand of the plaintiff, he returns to the claim in its entirety or part of it): i.e. if part of the compensation is taken from the plaintiff's hand, he returns to the claim for the share of what was taken of the settlement; and if all of it is taken, he returns to the claim for the whole. And in sulh with acknowledgment, if the compensation is taken, he returns to the substitute (the subject matter itself) due to the acknowledgment of the defendant; and in silence and denial, he returns to the claim for the substitute. [1] His saying: 'And whatever is taken...' means: whatever of the claimed property is taken in whole or in part in the case of sulh with silence or denial, the plaintiff returns to the defendant his share of the compensation, and the plaintiff returns to litigation with the claimant regarding what he claimed, whether in whole or in part. Its example: A man claimed a house in the possession of another man, and he denied or remained silent, then he settled for it for one hundred dirhams, so the one hundred came into the plaintiff's hand and the house into the defendant's hand, then all or part of the house was taken (by a third party). So the plaintiff returns the one hundred if all the house is taken, or fifty if half of it is taken, to the defendant, and he returns to litigation regarding the house with the claimant, because he (the plaintiff) took it (the compensation) on the basis of his claim as compensation for what he claimed. Then if that is taken, the defendant (the third party) returns to him (i.e., the plaintiff) on the basis of his claim, as if he bought it from him. And because the defendant only paid the compensation to remove litigation from himself and so that the claimed property remain in his hand without anyone litigating, so if it is taken, his objective is not achieved. (2) His saying: 'And whatever of the compensation is taken...' i.e., whatever of the compensation is taken in whole or in part, the plaintiff returns to his claim to its extent: if all is taken, he returns to the whole claim; if part is taken, he returns to part. Because the plaintiff only abandoned the claim to receive the compensation, and if it is not received, he returns to the substitute which is the claim. Contrary to if the sulh occurred with the wording of sale, such as one saying: 'I sell you this thing for this,' and the other saying: 'I bought,' where when the thing is taken (by a third party), the plaintiff (the seller) returns to the defendant (the buyer) with the claimed property itself, not with the claim, because the defendant's entering into the sale is an acknowledgment that the claimed property belongs to the plaintiff, so his denial is not considered, unlike sulh, because there is nothing from him indicating that he acknowledged ownership, since sulh may occur to remove litigation. This is mentioned in al-Tabyin and others.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of sulh, specifically addressing the situation where a third party (mustahiqq) proves rightful ownership to either the subject matter of the settlement (mudda'a) or the compensation (badal). The author explains two distinct rules. First: If the claimed property (mudda'a) is taken from the defendant by the third party, the plaintiff must return to the defendant the corresponding portion of the compensation he received. The plaintiff then pursues the third party by litigation over that property, since he claimed it originally. The rationale is that the defendant only paid the compensation to remove litigation from himself; if the property is taken by another, his purpose is defeated, so he gets his compensation back. The text gives an example: a plaintiff claims a house, settles for 100 dirhams after the defendant denies or remains silent, then a third party proves ownership of the whole or half the house. The plaintiff must return the full 100 or 50 dirhams to the defendant and then litigate with the third party. Second: If the compensation (badal) is taken from the plaintiff by a third party, the plaintiff reverts to his original claim against the defendant. This is because the plaintiff only gave up his claim in expectation of receiving the compensation; if that compensation is lost due to a superior claim, his basis for abandoning the claim disappears, so he returns to his claim. The author distinguishes a case where the sulh is phrased as a sale (bai'). In that case, if the compensation is taken, the plaintiff does not revert to his claim but rather claims the original property itself from the defendant, because the defendant's agreement to a sale is an acknowledgment that the property belongs to the plaintiff, so he is bound by that. This contrasts with ordinary sulh where the defendant's silence or denial does not amount to acknowledgment. The passage thus clarifies the consequences of third-party claims in settlement contracts, emphasizing the intent of the parties and the distinctions based on the form of the contract.

Key Terms
المدعى (al-mudda'a): The property or right claimed by the plaintiff, which is the subject of the lawsuit and settlement.
البدل (al-badal): The compensation or consideration given by the defendant to the plaintiff in a settlement (sulh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The plaintiff sues the third party for the compensation.
B) The plaintiff returns the compensation to the defendant and sues the third party for the property.
C) The plaintiff reverts to his original claim against the defendant.
D) The settlement becomes void and the property returns to its original owner.

Key Takeaway
In sulh, if the claimed property is taken, the plaintiff returns the compensation and pursues the true owner; if the compensation is taken, he reverts to his original claim against the defendant.

Sulh Over Property and Usufruct: The Condition of Different Types
States ruling and conditions for sulh over mal and manfa'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh over property and usufruct, and determine when a sulh over usufructs is valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Sulh over usufruct is valid only if the exchanged usufructs are of different types; same-type exchange is invalid, analogous to ijarah.

Sulh (compromise) is a valuable tool for resolving disputes without litigation. But its conditions differ depending on whether the claim involves property (mal) or usufruct (manfa'ah). This passage from the Hanafi tradition clarifies that while sulh over property is unconditionally valid, sulh over usufruct requires careful attention: you cannot exchange a usufruct for its own type, just as you cannot lease a usufruct for its own kind. This legal analogy prevents riba and ensures fairness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the core statement: 'Valid is sulh regarding a claim of property and usufruct'. This is the general rule. Note that 'valid' here means sahih (legally effective).
The ruling is unconditional for property but conditional for usufruct.
2
Understand the analogy for property
The author explains that sulh over property is analogous to a sale (bay'). When the sulh occurs upon acknowledgment, it is like a sale for both parties; when upon denial, it serves to redeem the oath and end litigation.
This analogy establishes that property transfers in sulh follow sale rules.
3
Understand the analogy for usufruct
Sulh over usufruct is analogous to ijarah (lease). Just as ijarah allows the exchange of usufruct for rent, sulh allows the exchange of a claimed usufruct for property or another usufruct, but with a critical condition.
The analogy to ijarah brings in the prohibition of riba al-fadl for same-type exchanges.
4
Apply the condition of different types
If a usufruct is exchanged for another usufruct, they must be of different types (jins). The passage gives examples: sulh for residence in exchange for the service of a slave is valid; sulh for residence in exchange for residence is invalid.
The condition arises because ijarah does not permit hiring a usufruct for its own kind.
5
Recognize the consequence
If the usufructs are of the same type, the sulh is invalid (batil). If they are of different types, it is valid. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
This ruling may differ from other schools, so note the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام الصلح (وصح الصلح عن دعوى المال والمنفعة) قيل : صورة الصلح عن دعوى المنفعة : أن يدعي على الورثة أن الميت كان أوصى بخدمة هذا العبد، وأنكر الورثة [1] قوله : وصح الصلح عن دعوى المال ؛ لأنه في معنى البيع في حقهما إن وقع عنه بمال عن إقرار، وفي حق المدعي وحده إن وقع عن إنكار أو سكوت، وفي حق الآخر؛ لافتداء اليمين وقطع الخصومة، وفي معنى الإجارة إن وقع عنه بمنافع، وكل ذلك جائز على ما مرّ. والمنفعة ؛ فإنّها تملك بعقد الإجارة، فكذا بالصلح، ألا ترى أن الورثة لو صالحوا الموصى له بالخدمة على مال أو منفعةٍ جاز ، فهذا أولى؛ لكونه معلوماً ؛ لأنّ لها مدة متناهية، لكن الصلح عن المنافع على المنفعة إنما يجوز إذا كانا مختلفي الجنس، بأن يصالح عن السكنى على خدمة العبد، أو زراعة الأرض، أو لبس الثياب. أما إذا اتحد جنسهما كما إذا صالح عن السكنى على السكني أو عن الزراعة على الزراعة فلا يجوز؛ لأنه لا يجوز استئجار المنفعة بجنسها من المنافع ، فكذا الصلح وعند اختلاف الجنس يجوز استئجارها بالمنفعة، فكذا الصلح. ذكره العيني، والزيلعي في شرح الكنز. [2]قوله : قيل.... الخ ؛ هكذا ذكره في «السراج الوهاج» نقلاً عن «المستصفى»، لكن ذكر في «البحر» : إنَّ الصلح عن دعوى المال مطلقاً والمنفعة جائز، كصلح المستأجر مع المؤجر عند إنكاره الإجارة أو المدة المدعى بها مقداراً والأجرة، وكذا الورثة إذا صالحوا الموصي له بالخدمة على مال مطلقاً، والمنافع إن اختلف جنسها، فإنّه يجوز، لا إن اتحد. انتهى.
Section on the types of sulh. (Valid is sulh regarding a claim of property and usufruct). It is said: The example of sulh regarding a claim of usufruct is: that he claims against the heirs that the deceased had bequeathed the service of this slave, and the heirs deny. [1] His saying: 'Valid is sulh regarding a claim of property' because it is in the sense of a sale with respect to both parties if it occurs for property upon acknowledgement, and with respect to the plaintiff alone if it occurs upon denial or silence, and with respect to the other party for redeeming the oath and ending litigation. And it is in the sense of ijarah if it occurs for usufructs. All that is permissible as previously mentioned. And usufruct: because it is owned by ijarah contract, so likewise by sulh. Do you not see that if the heirs make sulh with the legatee of service for property or usufruct, it is permissible; so this is more appropriate because it is known, for it has a finite period. However, sulh over usufructs for usufruct is only permissible if they are of different types, such as making sulh for residence in exchange for the service of a slave, or cultivation of land, or wearing clothes. But if they are of the same type, such as sulh for residence in exchange for residence, or for cultivation in exchange for cultivation, it is not permissible; because it is not permissible to hire a usufruct for its same type of usufruct, and likewise sulh. When the types differ, it is permissible to hire it for a usufruct, and likewise sulh. Mentioned by al-'Ayni and al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz. [2] His saying: 'It is said...' etc.; thus it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj quoting from al-Mustasfa, but it is mentioned in al-Bahr: Indeed, sulh regarding a claim of property unconditionally and usufruct is permissible, like the sulh of the lessee with the lessor when he denies the lease or the claimed period of amount and rent, and likewise the heirs if they make sulh with the legatee of service for property unconditionally, and for usufructs if their types differ, then it is permissible, but not if they are the same. End.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This section explains the validity of sulh (compromise) in claims involving property (mal) and usufruct (manfa'ah). The matn states that sulh is valid for both. The sharh provides the legal basis: sulh over property is analogous to a sale (bay') when it involves a property exchange upon acknowledgment, or when it is upon denial, it serves to redeem the oath and end litigation. Sulh over usufruct is analogous to ijarah (lease). The key condition is that if usufruct is exchanged for usufruct, the two usufructs must be of different types (different jins). For example, sulh for residence in exchange for the service of a slave is valid, but sulh for residence in exchange for residence is invalid, just as ijarah does not permit hiring a usufruct for its own kind. This principle is cited from al-'Ayni and al-Zayla'i. The passage also quotes al-Bahr al-Ra'iq which confirms that sulh over property is unconditionally valid, and over usufructs it is valid only if the types differ.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise settlement to end a dispute, often involving exchange of property or usufruct.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Usufruct or benefit derived from an asset.
جنس (jins): Type or category of usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on sulh for residence in exchange for cultivation of land, according to Hanafi law?
A) Valid, because they are different types of usufruct
B) Invalid, because both are usufructs
C) Valid only if the period is the same
D) Invalid, because cultivation is not a valid usufruct

Key Takeaway
Sulh over usufruct is valid only when the exchanged usufructs are of different types; same-type exchange is invalid by analogy to ijarah, preventing riba.

Sulh in Qisas and Diyah: Permissibility and Conditions
Explains permissibility and conditions of sulh in qisas and diyah claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh in qisas, distinguish it from sulh in debt claims regarding riba, and apply the conditions for valid compensation.

Core Idea
In qisas, compensation can exceed the diyah because the obligation is not wealth-based, thus no riba applies.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi treatment of compromise (sulh) in cases of intentional killing (qisas) and accidental killing (diyah). You will see how the Law permits flexibility in compensation while upholding the prohibition of riba. The key is whether the underlying obligation is a fixed financial right or a non-financial penal right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim type
Determine whether the claim is for qisas (intentional act) or diyah (accidental). This dictates whether the obligation is non-financial (qisas) or financial (diyah).
The text explicitly distinguishes between 'amd (intentional) and khata' (accidental).
2
Recognize the ruling on sulh
State that sulh in qisas is permissible and the compensation can be more or less than the diyah amount. For diyah, increase from the same type is not allowed due to riba.
The author uses qiyas with marriage and debt to explain.
3
Analyze the condition of compensation
Check if the compensation is known (ma'lum), if it is from a different type or same type, and if it involves riba when the obligation is financial.
If the compromise is on a type that is ribawi and the same as the original obligation, increase is riba unless the obligation is non-financial.
4
Apply the possession condition
If the compensation is a debt in the liability (dayn fi al-dhimmah), possession must occur in the session to avoid a debt-for-debt exchange.
This is a specific condition derived from hadith prohibiting 'kali' bi kali'.

الصلح تعريفه وأقسامه
وإنما قيل : شيء من العفو ؛ ليعلم أنه إذا عفا عن بعض الدم أو عفا عنه بعض الورثة تم العفو، وسقط القصاص، ومن فسَّرَ عفى بترك جعل شيء مفعولاً به، وكذا من فسّره بأعطى يعنى أنّ الولد إذا أعطي له شيء من مال أخيه يعني القاتل، بطريق الصلح ، فليأخذه بمعروف من غير تعنيف، وليؤدِّه القاتل إليه بلا تسويف. انتهى. ولأنه حق ثابت في المحلّ في حق الفعل، فجازَ أخذ العوض عنه، كملك النكاح ، وما جاز أن يكون مهراً جاز أن يكون بدل الصلح ، وذلك مثل الأمور المعلومة، والمنافع المعلومة، وما لا يصح مهراً لا يصلح بدلاً عن القود، مثل الخمر والخنزير. لكن في النكاح يجب مهر المثل ؛ لأن النكاح لم يشرع بلا مال والعفو مشروع بدونه مندوب إليه ؛ ولهذا لو لم يسم شيئاً فيهما يجب في النكاح مهر المثل ؛ لأنَّ البضعَ متقوم حالة الدخول، ومهر المثل قيمةٌ له؛ لأنه هو الموجب الأصلي، وفي العفو عن القود لا يجب شيء ؛ لأنه لا يتقوم إلا بالتقويم ولم يوجد ؛ وهذا لأن التقويم يكون بقيام غيره مقامه. والقصاص لا يقوم غيره مقامه ؛ إذ لا يماثله غيره إلا أنَّ الشرع أجاز عوضه عند اتفاقهما، فجاز أخذه، وأما الخطأ في النفس ؛ فلأنَّ موجبه المال، والصلح عن دعواه جائز كما تقدم، إلا أنه تصحُ الزيادة على قدر الدية إذا وقع الصلح على أحد مقادير الدية للربا، كما لا يجوز الصلح على أكثر من الدين من جنسه في دعوى الدين. بخلاف الصلح عن القود، حيث تجوزُ الزيادة فيه على قدر الدية، وكذا على الأقل، وإن كان أقل من عشرة دراهم ؛ لأنه لا موجب له في المال، وإنما يجب بالعقد، فيتقدر بتقديرهما، بخلاف النكاح حيث لا يجوز تسمية ما دون العشرة فيه ؛ لأنه مقدر به شرعاً. ولو وقع الصلحُ على غير مقادير الدية جاز كيفما كان ؛ لعدم الربا إلا أنه يشترط القبض في المجلس إذا كان ما وقع عليه الصلح ديناً في الذمة كيلا يكون افتراقاً عن كالي بكالئ، ولو قضى القاضي بأخذ مقادير الدِّيةِ فصالح على جنس آخر منها بالزيادة جاز ؛ لأنَّ الحق تعين فيه بالقضاء، فكان غيره من مقادير الدِّيةِ كجنس آخر، فأمكن الحمل على المعاوضة.

والرق، ودعوى الزوج النكاح ، وكان عتقاً بمال وخلعاً) : أي إن كان الصلح على مال عن دعوى الرق كان عتقا بمال [٣] بخلاف الصلح عليه ابتداءً ؛ لأنّ تراضيهما على بعض المقادير بمنزلة قضاء القاضي، فكما لا يجوز للقاضي أن يقضي بالزيادة على الدِّيةِ من جنسه لا يجوز لهما أيضاً أن يصطلحا عليها لما يلزم من الزنا، وأما ما دون النفس فمعتبر بالنفس، فيلحق ما يوجب القصاص فيه بالعمد، وما يوجب المال فيه بالخطأ فيها).

[١]قوله : والرق ؛ يعني وصح الصلح أيضاً عن دعوى الرق، كما إذا ادعى على مجهول النسب أنه عبده ، ثمَّ تصالحا على شيء معين جاز هذا الصلح، وكان عتقاً بمال في حق المدعي. وفي حق الآخر لدفع الخصومة ؛ لأنه أمكن تصحيحه بهذا الاعتبار فصح ولا ولاء له عليه ؛ لإنكار العبد إلا أن يقيم المدعي البينة بعد ذلك، فتقبل في حق ثبوت الولاء عليه لا غير هذا إذا أنكر العبد الرق، وأما اذا صالحه بإقراره فيثبت الولاء. [٢] قوله : ودعوى الزوج النكاح ؛ أي وصح الصلح عن دعوى الزوج النكاح ، وكان خلعاً مطلقاً في زعمهما إن كان بإقرار، فتجب عليها العدة، وإن لم يكن بإقرار يكون خلعاً في زعمه ودفعاً في زعمها، ولا تلزم العدة عليها قضاء، فإن أقام على التزويج بينة بعد الصلح لم تقبل، ويحرم أخذ المال على المدعي ديانة إن كان مبطلاً في دعواه، وهذا عام في جميع أنواع الصلح إلا أن يسلّمه بطيب نفسه، فيكون تمليكاً على طريق الهبة. صرح به في ((العناية))) ولو صالحها بمال لتقرَّ له بالنكاح جاز، وتجعل زيادة في المهر ؛ لأنها تزعم أنها زوجـت نـفـسـهـا مـنـه ابتداء بالمسمّى، وهو يزعم أنه زاد في مهـرها. ذكره في «مجمع الأنهر» وغيره.

[٣] قوله : كان عتقاً بمال ؛ لأنه أمكن تصحيحه على هذا الوجه ؛ لأنه أقرب العقود إليه شبهاً بالعتق على مال، فيجعل في معناه.
The compromise: its definition and types. It is said 'something of forgiveness' so that it is known that if one forgives part of the blood or some of the heirs forgive, the forgiveness is complete and qisas drops. And who interprets 'afa' as 'leave' makes something an object; likewise who interprets it as 'give' means that if the child is given something from the property of his brother, meaning the killer, by way of compromise, then let him take it with kindness without harshness, and let the killer pay it to him without delay. End. And because it is a right established in the subject regarding the act, so taking compensation for it is permissible, like ownership of marriage. And whatever is permissible as a dowry is permissible as a substitute for compromise, such as known objects and known benefits. And what is not valid as a dowry is not suitable as a substitute for qisas, such as wine and swine. But in marriage, the dower of the like is obligatory because marriage is not legislated without wealth, while forgiveness is legislated without it and is recommended. Hence if nothing is named in either, the dower of the like is obligatory in marriage because the vulva is valuable at the time of entry, and the dower of the like is its value because it is the original obligation. In forgiveness of qisas, nothing is obligatory because it is not valuable except by valuation, and it did not occur. This is because valuation is by something else taking its place; qisas cannot be replaced by anything else, as nothing resembles it, except that the Law permitted its substitute when they agree, so taking it is permissible. As for error in a life, its requirement is wealth, and compromise on its claim is permissible as earlier, except that increase over the amount of diyah is not valid if the compromise is on one of the amounts of diyah due to riba, just as compromise for more than the debt of its kind is not allowed in a debt claim. Unlike compromise for qisas, where increase over the amount of diyah is allowed, and likewise decrease, even if less than ten dirhams, because it has no requirement in wealth and is only obligatory by contract, so it is determined by their determination, unlike marriage where naming less than ten is not allowed because it is determined by law. And if the compromise is on other than the amounts of diyah, it is valid however it is due to absence of riba, but possession in the session is required if what the compromise is upon is a debt in the liability so that it is not a parting from a debt with a debt. And if the judge ruled to take the amounts of diyah and then he compromised on another kind with an increase, it is valid because the right became determined by the ruling, so other than it from the amounts of diyah is like another kind, so it can be carried upon exchange.

And slavery and the husband's claim of marriage, and it was emancipation for wealth and khul'. That is, if the compromise is for wealth upon a claim of slavery, it is emancipation for wealth. Unlike compromise upon it initially, because their mutual agreement on some amounts is like the ruling of the judge. Just as it is not permissible for the judge to rule for increase over the diyah of its kind, it is also not permissible for them to compromise on it due to riba. And what is less than a life is considered with the life, so what requires qisas follows intentional, and what requires wealth follows error therein.

[1] His saying: 'And slavery' means the compromise is also valid upon a claim of slavery, as if one claims of unknown lineage that he is his slave, then they compromise on something specific, this compromise is valid, and it is emancipation for wealth regarding the claimant. And regarding the other, it is to avoid litigation, because it is possible to validate it by this consideration, so it is valid and no wala' is established for him due to the slave's denial, unless the claimant later establishes proof, then it is accepted regarding establishing wala' upon him only. This is if the slave denies slavery. But if he compromises with his acknowledgment, then wala' is established. [2] His saying: And the husband's claim of marriage means the compromise is valid upon the husband's claim of marriage, and it is an absolute khul' in their assumption if it is with acknowledgment, then 'iddah is obligatory upon her. And if it is not with acknowledgment, it is khul' in his assumption and repulsion in her assumption, and 'iddah is not obligatory upon her judicially. If he establishes proof of marriage after the compromise, it is not accepted. And it is unlawful for the claimant to take the money religion-wise if he is false in his claim. This is general in all types of compromise, unless he gives it willingly, then it is a gift. Declared in al-'Inayah. And if he compromises with her for wealth so that she acknowledges the marriage for him, it is valid and is made an increase in the dowry, because she claims that she married herself to him initially with the named dower, and he claims that he increased her dower. Mentioned in Majma' al-Anhur and others.

[3] His saying: it was emancipation for wealth because it is possible to validate it in this way because it is the contract closest to it in resemblance to emancipation for wealth, so it is made in its meaning.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah, discussing the rulings of sulh (compromise) in the context of qisas (retaliation) and blood money. The text begins by explaining the meaning of 'something of forgiveness' in the Quranic verse regarding qisas. It clarifies that if the victim's heirs forgive part or all of the blood money, qisas is waived. The author then provides a legal analogy: since qisas is a right that can be waived, taking compensation for it is permissible, similar to marriage where dowry is taken in exchange for marital rights. However, there is a key distinction: in marriage, if no dower is specified, the dower of the like is obligatory because marriage is not legislated without wealth. In contrast, forgiveness of qisas is recommended even without compensation; hence nothing is obligatory unless agreed. The text then addresses the difference between compromise in intentional killing (ammd) and accidental killing (khat'). In intentional killing, the only requirement is qisas, so compensation is determined by mutual agreement and can exceed the diyah amount without falling into riba. In accidental killing, the requirement is wealth (diyah), so compromise on a known amount of diyah is valid, but increasing it from the same type would be riba. The passage also discusses the conditions for receiving compensation: if the compromise is on a debt in the liability, possession must occur in the session to avoid a debt-for-debt exchange. Additionally, if the judge has already ruled for diyah, subsequent compromise on a different type with increase is valid. The second part of the passage discusses application to claims of slavery and marriage. If someone claims another as his slave and they compromise on a payment, it is treated as emancipation for wealth in favor of the claimant, and the supposed slave is considered free without wala' unless he acknowledges the claim. For a husband's claim of marriage, if the wife denies and they compromise on payment, the compromise functions as khul' if the husband's claim is acknowledged, requiring 'iddah; otherwise it is a mere repulsion without 'iddah. The text emphasizes that the ruling is based on making the contract valid by interpreting it as the closest analogous contract (e.g., emancipation for wealth or khul') to uphold the compromise.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad): Retaliation (qisas) for intentional killing or wounding; the right to exact retribution.
الصلح (al-sulh): A contract of compromise or settlement between disputing parties, often involving payment to drop a claim.
الربا (al-riba): Usury or unlawful increase, particularly in exchanges of the same type of weighed or measured items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to compromise for an amount exceeding the diyah in a qisas case (intentional killing) but not in a debt claim?
A) Because qisas is not a financial obligation, so no riba applies; debt is financial, so riba applies.
B) Because the diyah amount is set by law, but qisas can be waived entirely, so any compensation is valid.
C) Because the parties can agree on any amount in qisas due to the absence of a legal cap.
D) Because qisas is a criminal matter, whereas debt is civil.

Key Takeaway
Sulh in qisas is permissible with any known compensation, even exceeding diyah, because the right is not financial; riba concerns only apply when the original obligation is wealth.

Sulh in Claims of Slavery and Marriage: Emancipation and Khul'
Explains sulh in claims of slavery and marriage, treating them as emancipation for wealth and khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how sulh in a claim of slavery is treated as emancipation for wealth, and how sulh in a marriage denial is treated as khul', and identify the conditions for each.

Core Idea
Sulh in slavery and marriage claims is validated by interpreting it as the closest analogous contract: emancipation for wealth and khul' respectively.

This lesson extends the principles of sulh to claims of slavery and marriage. When someone claims another is a slave or a spouse, and they compromise on payment, the law constructs the transaction as the nearest valid contract—emancipation for wealth or khul'. This preserves the compromise while respecting the rights of the parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Determine whether the underlying claim is for slavery or marriage. In slavery, the claimant asserts ownership; in marriage, the claimant asserts spousal rights.
The text covers both scenarios.
2
Apply the implicit contract construction
Since a direct sulh on such personal status claims may be inappropriate, the law treats it as the closest valid contract: for slavery, it becomes 'itq bi mal' (emancipation for wealth); for marriage, it becomes khul' (divorce by compensation).
This is based on the principle of making the transaction valid (tashih) by analogy.
3
Determine the effect on wala' and 'iddah
If the sulh is with acknowledgment, wala' is established for the claimant in slavery, and 'iddah is required in marriage. If without acknowledgment, wala' is denied and 'iddah is not due judicially.
The text explicitly addresses these consequences.
4
Note the prohibition of taking money if the claim is false
If the claimant is false (batil) in his claim, it is haram to take the money in the sight of God (diyanatan), unless he gives it willingly as a gift.
This is a general ruling for all sulh.

وإنما قيل : شيء من العفو ؛ ليعلم أنه إذا عفا عن بعض الدم أو عفا عنه بعض الورثة تم العفو، وسقط القصاص، ومن فسَّرَ عفى بترك جعل شيء مفعولاً به، وكذا من فسّره بأعطى يعنى أنّ الولد إذا أعطي له شيء من مال أخيه يعني القاتل، بطريق الصلح ، فليأخذه بمعروف من غير تعنيف، وليؤدِّه القاتل إليه بلا تسويف. انتهى. ولأنه حق ثابت في المحلّ في حق الفعل، فجازَ أخذ العوض عنه، كملك النكاح ، وما جاز أن يكون مهراً جاز أن يكون بدل الصلح ، وذلك مثل الأمور المعلومة، والمنافع المعلومة، وما لا يصح مهراً لا يصلح بدلاً عن القود، مثل الخمر والخنزير. لكن في النكاح يجب مهر المثل ؛ لأن النكاح لم يشرع بلا مال والعفو مشروع بدونه مندوب إليه ؛ ولهذا لو لم يسم شيئاً فيهما يجب في النكاح مهر المثل ؛ لأنَّ البضعَ متقوم حالة الدخول، ومهر المثل قيمةٌ له؛ لأنه هو الموجب الأصلي، وفي العفو عن القود لا يجب شيء ؛ لأنه لا يتقوم إلا بالتقويم ولم يوجد ؛ وهذا لأن التقويم يكون بقيام غيره مقامه. والقصاص لا يقوم غيره مقامه ؛ إذ لا يماثله غيره إلا أنَّ الشرع أجاز عوضه عند اتفاقهما، فجاز أخذه، وأما الخطأ في النفس ؛ فلأنَّ موجبه المال، والصلح عن دعواه جائز كما تقدم، إلا أنه تصحُ الزيادة على قدر الدية إذا وقع الصلح على أحد مقادير الدية للربا، كما لا يجوز الصلح على أكثر من الدين من جنسه في دعوى الدين. بخلاف الصلح عن القود، حيث تجوزُ الزيادة فيه على قدر الدية، وكذا على الأقل، وإن كان أقل من عشرة دراهم ؛ لأنه لا موجب له في المال، وإنما يجب بالعقد، فيتقدر بتقديرهما، بخلاف النكاح حيث لا يجوز تسمية ما دون العشرة فيه ؛ لأنه مقدر به شرعاً. ولو وقع الصلحُ على غير مقادير الدية جاز كيفما كان ؛ لعدم الربا إلا أنه يشترط القبض في المجلس إذا كان ما وقع عليه الصلح ديناً في الذمة كيلا يكون افتراقاً عن كالي بكالئ، ولو قضى القاضي بأخذ مقادير الدِّيةِ فصالح على جنس آخر منها بالزيادة جاز ؛ لأنَّ الحق تعين فيه بالقضاء، فكان غيره من مقادير الدِّيةِ كجنس آخر، فأمكن الحمل على المعاوضة.

والرق، ودعوى الزوج النكاح ، وكان عتقاً بمال وخلعاً) : أي إن كان الصلح على مال عن دعوى الرق كان عتقا بمال [٣] بخلاف الصلح عليه ابتداءً ؛ لأنّ تراضيهما على بعض المقادير بمنزلة قضاء القاضي، فكما لا يجوز للقاضي أن يقضي بالزيادة على الدِّيةِ من جنسه لا يجوز لهما أيضاً أن يصطلحا عليها لما يلزم من الزنا، وأما ما دون النفس فمعتبر بالنفس، فيلحق ما يوجب القصاص فيه بالعمد، وما يوجب المال فيه بالخطأ فيها).

[١]قوله : والرق ؛ يعني وصح الصلح أيضاً عن دعوى الرق، كما إذا ادعى على مجهول النسب أنه عبده ، ثمَّ تصالحا على شيء معين جاز هذا الصلح، وكان عتقاً بمال في حق المدعي. وفي حق الآخر لدفع الخصومة ؛ لأنه أمكن تصحيحه بهذا الاعتبار فصح ولا ولاء له عليه ؛ لإنكار العبد إلا أن يقيم المدعي البينة بعد ذلك، فتقبل في حق ثبوت الولاء عليه لا غير هذا إذا أنكر العبد الرق، وأما اذا صالحه بإقراره فيثبت الولاء. [٢] قوله : ودعوى الزوج النكاح ؛ أي وصح الصلح عن دعوى الزوج النكاح ، وكان خلعاً مطلقاً في زعمهما إن كان بإقرار، فتجب عليها العدة، وإن لم يكن بإقرار يكون خلعاً في زعمه ودفعاً في زعمها، ولا تلزم العدة عليها قضاء، فإن أقام على التزويج بينة بعد الصلح لم تقبل، ويحرم أخذ المال على المدعي ديانة إن كان مبطلاً في دعواه، وهذا عام في جميع أنواع الصلح إلا أن يسلّمه بطيب نفسه، فيكون تمليكاً على طريق الهبة. صرح به في ((العناية))) ولو صالحها بمال لتقرَّ له بالنكاح جاز، وتجعل زيادة في المهر ؛ لأنها تزعم أنها زوجـت نـفـسـهـا مـنـه ابتداء بالمسمّى، وهو يزعم أنه زاد في مهـرها. ذكره في «مجمع الأنهر» وغيره.

[٣] قوله : كان عتقاً بمال ؛ لأنه أمكن تصحيحه على هذا الوجه ؛ لأنه أقرب العقود إليه شبهاً بالعتق على مال، فيجعل في معناه.
The compromise: its definition and types. It is said 'something of forgiveness' so that it is known that if one forgives part of the blood or some of the heirs forgive, the forgiveness is complete and qisas drops. And who interprets 'afa' as 'leave' makes something an object; likewise who interprets it as 'give' means that if the child is given something from the property of his brother, meaning the killer, by way of compromise, then let him take it with kindness without harshness, and let the killer pay it to him without delay. End. And because it is a right established in the subject regarding the act, so taking compensation for it is permissible, like ownership of marriage. And whatever is permissible as a dowry is permissible as a substitute for compromise, such as known objects and known benefits. And what is not valid as a dowry is not suitable as a substitute for qisas, such as wine and swine. But in marriage, the dower of the like is obligatory because marriage is not legislated without wealth, while forgiveness is legislated without it and is recommended. Hence if nothing is named in either, the dower of the like is obligatory in marriage because the vulva is valuable at the time of entry, and the dower of the like is its value because it is the original obligation. In forgiveness of qisas, nothing is obligatory because it is not valuable except by valuation, and it did not occur. This is because valuation is by something else taking its place; qisas cannot be replaced by anything else, as nothing resembles it, except that the Law permitted its substitute when they agree, so taking it is permissible. As for error in a life, its requirement is wealth, and compromise on its claim is permissible as earlier, except that increase over the amount of diyah is not valid if the compromise is on one of the amounts of diyah due to riba, just as compromise for more than the debt of its kind is not allowed in a debt claim. Unlike compromise for qisas, where increase over the amount of diyah is allowed, and likewise decrease, even if less than ten dirhams, because it has no requirement in wealth and is only obligatory by contract, so it is determined by their determination, unlike marriage where naming less than ten is not allowed because it is determined by law. And if the compromise is on other than the amounts of diyah, it is valid however it is due to absence of riba, but possession in the session is required if what the compromise is upon is a debt in the liability so that it is not a parting from a debt with a debt. And if the judge ruled to take the amounts of diyah and then he compromised on another kind with an increase, it is valid because the right became determined by the ruling, so other than it from the amounts of diyah is like another kind, so it can be carried upon exchange.

And slavery and the husband's claim of marriage, and it was emancipation for wealth and khul'. That is, if the compromise is for wealth upon a claim of slavery, it is emancipation for wealth. Unlike compromise upon it initially, because their mutual agreement on some amounts is like the ruling of the judge. Just as it is not permissible for the judge to rule for increase over the diyah of its kind, it is also not permissible for them to compromise on it due to riba. And what is less than a life is considered with the life, so what requires qisas follows intentional, and what requires wealth follows error therein.

[1] His saying: 'And slavery' means the compromise is also valid upon a claim of slavery, as if one claims of unknown lineage that he is his slave, then they compromise on something specific, this compromise is valid, and it is emancipation for wealth regarding the claimant. And regarding the other, it is to avoid litigation, because it is possible to validate it by this consideration, so it is valid and no wala' is established for him due to the slave's denial, unless the claimant later establishes proof, then it is accepted regarding establishing wala' upon him only. This is if the slave denies slavery. But if he compromises with his acknowledgment, then wala' is established. [2] His saying: And the husband's claim of marriage means the compromise is valid upon the husband's claim of marriage, and it is an absolute khul' in their assumption if it is with acknowledgment, then 'iddah is obligatory upon her. And if it is not with acknowledgment, it is khul' in his assumption and repulsion in her assumption, and 'iddah is not obligatory upon her judicially. If he establishes proof of marriage after the compromise, it is not accepted. And it is unlawful for the claimant to take the money religion-wise if he is false in his claim. This is general in all types of compromise, unless he gives it willingly, then it is a gift. Declared in al-'Inayah. And if he compromises with her for wealth so that she acknowledges the marriage for him, it is valid and is made an increase in the dowry, because she claims that she married herself to him initially with the named dower, and he claims that he increased her dower. Mentioned in Majma' al-Anhur and others.

[3] His saying: it was emancipation for wealth because it is possible to validate it in this way because it is the contract closest to it in resemblance to emancipation for wealth, so it is made in its meaning.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah, discussing the rulings of sulh (compromise) in the context of qisas (retaliation) and blood money. The text begins by explaining the meaning of 'something of forgiveness' in the Quranic verse regarding qisas. It clarifies that if the victim's heirs forgive part or all of the blood money, qisas is waived. The author then provides a legal analogy: since qisas is a right that can be waived, taking compensation for it is permissible, similar to marriage where dowry is taken in exchange for marital rights. However, there is a key distinction: in marriage, if no dower is specified, the dower of the like is obligatory because marriage is not legislated without wealth. In contrast, forgiveness of qisas is recommended even without compensation; hence nothing is obligatory unless agreed. The text then addresses the difference between compromise in intentional killing (ammd) and accidental killing (khat'). In intentional killing, the only requirement is qisas, so compensation is determined by mutual agreement and can exceed the diyah amount without falling into riba. In accidental killing, the requirement is wealth (diyah), so compromise on a known amount of diyah is valid, but increasing it from the same type would be riba. The passage also discusses the conditions for receiving compensation: if the compromise is on a debt in the liability, possession must occur in the session to avoid a debt-for-debt exchange. Additionally, if the judge has already ruled for diyah, subsequent compromise on a different type with increase is valid. The second part of the passage discusses application to claims of slavery and marriage. If someone claims another as his slave and they compromise on a payment, it is treated as emancipation for wealth in favor of the claimant, and the supposed slave is considered free without wala' unless he acknowledges the claim. For a husband's claim of marriage, if the wife denies and they compromise on payment, the compromise functions as khul' if the husband's claim is acknowledged, requiring 'iddah; otherwise it is a mere repulsion without 'iddah. The text emphasizes that the ruling is based on making the contract valid by interpreting it as the closest analogous contract (e.g., emancipation for wealth or khul') to uphold the compromise.

Key Terms
العتق بمال (al-'itq bi mal): Emancipation of a slave in exchange for payment from the slave or a third party.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in return for compensation paid to the husband.
الولاء (al-wala'): Patronage right established between the emancipator and the freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh on a husband's claim of marriage where the wife denies, which condition makes 'iddah obligatory?
A) If the husband acknowledges his own claim (i.e., asserts it genuinely)
B) If the wife acknowledges
C) In all cases
D) Only if a judge orders it

Key Takeaway
Sulh in slavery and marriage claims is validated by interpreting it as the nearest permissible contract, preserving both the compromise and the Shari'ah.
